Is it possible to do the GBP posts in bulk? How's the API, can I access it right away or does it take weeks?
Yes, bulk GBP posts are possible via the API — but there's a catch worth knowing before you film this:

The access problem:
Google Business Profile API requires you to submit an access request and get approved. It's not instant — can take 2-4 weeks, sometimes longer. It's not like YouTube Data API where you get a key immediately.

What that means for your video:
If your audience can't replicate it day one, it weakens the "do this now" angle. Worth flagging in the video or building a workaround into the demo.

Workarounds to consider:

Playwright automation — log in as the business, post via the GBP dashboard UI. No API approval needed, works immediately
Third-party tools — some scheduling tools (like Publer, Semrush) have GBP API access baked in — Claude Code generates the posts, you paste/import
Batch creation + manual upload — Claude Code generates 30 posts in a JSON file, client uploads via GBP's bulk import (limited but exists)
My honest take:
The Playwright route is probably the cleanest for a video — you can show it working live without the API wait, and it's more accessible to your audience.

What is the step by step instructions to add someone to a gmb profile?
To add someone to a Google Business Profile:

Go to business.google.com and sign in
Select the business
Click the three dots (top right) → Business Profile settings
Click Managers
Click the Add button (person+ icon)
Enter their Google email address
Choose their role:
Owner — full control, can delete the listing
Manager — can post, reply to reviews, edit profile (what you want as a freelancer)
Site Manager — very limited, avoid this
Click Invite
They get an email, accept it, done
For your video context:

When onboarding a client, you want Manager access — not Owner. Owner can remove you, and you don't need that level anyway.

Worth including a 60-second "client onboarding" clip in the crash course showing exactly this — it's the first thing someone does when they land a local SEO client and most people don't know where to find it.

Also worth noting: if the client is slow to add you, Make.com scenarios can be built with the client's credentials instead — just means they need to authenticate it themselves during setup.

Ok, can I access historical GMB views through google analytics or google search console?
Google Search Console — yes, but limited:

Impressions and clicks from Google Search
Not GBP-specific (maps views, direction requests, calls)
Google Analytics — only if you've linked it and someone clicks through to your website from GBP. It won't show profile views, map views, or calls.

The best source for GBP performance data is GBP itself:

business.google.com → Performance tab
Shows: search views, map views, direction requests, calls, website clicks
Goes back 6 months historically
This is what you'd pull for client reporting
The gap: GBP's API does expose this performance data, so you could pull it via Make.com and log it to a Google Sheet over time — building historical data beyond the 6-month window. That's actually a strong piece to include in the crash course as part of the reporting module.

Research done — 64 tool uses, 45+ sources read in full. Here's what's genuinely missing or new that changes the video:

Things we hadn't covered that matter:

1. Q&A section is dead
Google phased it out starting December 2025, replacing with AI-generated answers. Don't teach it. Teach FAQ content on the website instead (that's what AI pulls from).

2. AI Overviews have zero proximity bias
This is massive. Traditional local pack = proximity-heavy. AI Overviews = pure content authority. A business 10 miles away with better content/reviews/citations beats you in AI results. Almost nobody is teaching this.

3. The "magic 10 reviews" threshold
Sterling Sky data: going from 9 → 10 reviews triggers a measurable ranking jump. After 10, velocity matters more than volume. Most people say "get more reviews" — the real advice is "get to 10 first, then stay consistent."

4. "Business open at time of search" is now a top 5 ranking factor
New in 2024-2025. If your profile says you're closed, you get filtered out. Extended hours = competitive advantage.

5. Removing attributes can help
Counter-intuitive: removing "onsite services" and "online appointment" attributes pushes your reviews back into view. Worth a 30-second mention.

6. Identity attributes create brand new ranking slots
Adding "Women-owned," "Veteran-owned," or "LGBTQ+ friendly" doesn't just filter searches — it creates local pack results for queries that previously had NO local pack. Completely untapped.

7. GBP suspensions have exploded
"More suspensions in the last year than the previous 15 years combined." Any video teaching GBP management needs a 2-minute segment on what gets you suspended and how to recover.

8. Which URL you link in GBP is a ranking factor
Linking to a page that already ranks organically can cause Google to demote your profile. Almost never discussed. Claude Code can audit this.

9. Posts don't directly improve rankings
Sterling Sky ran a 9-week controlled test. Zero measurable ranking impact. Still worth posting for engagement/conversion reasons — but don't promise ranking improvements from posting.

10. Citations are making a comeback specifically for AI search
The "citations are dead" narrative is wrong. Whitespark 2026 survey explicitly called this out — AI systems pull from Yelp, Facebook, directories to build business profiles. Consistent citations across platforms = more AI recommendations.

All three are great points. Let me address each:

1. Localized blog posts — yes, this is a major missing section

This is actually one of the strongest plays for Claude Code because it scales infinitely. It's also how you rank for high-intent searches that aren't your direct service.

Examples:

Wedding videographer ranks for "best wedding venues in Vancouver" → captures couples in planning mode → converts them on the videography service
Marketing agency ranks for "best coffee shops in Toronto for meetings" → captures business owners → soft-converts to consultations
HVAC company ranks for "best neighborhoods to buy a home in [city]" → captures movers → upsells HVAC inspections
What Claude Code can do here:

Generate 50 "best X in [city]" posts from one template
Pull real businesses via Google Places API + scrape competitor lists
Generate proper schema (ItemList, LocalBusiness for each entry)
Internal link back to your service pages
Auto-update annually (Make.com triggered)
Where this goes in the outline: New Part 4 (between location landing pages and Claude Code section). I'd call it "The Blog Engine" or "Hyperlocal Content at Scale."

2. Review filter system — yes, but flag the nuance

The exact flow you want:

Email to all clients → simple rating form (1-5 stars)
4-5 stars → "Mind leaving us a Google review?" with direct review link
1-3 stars → internal feedback form → emails you/team
The catch you should know: Google's TOS technically forbids "review gating" (routing only happy customers to Google). Most businesses do it anyway and Google rarely enforces, but worth mentioning honestly in the video — your audience deserves to know the risk.

The compliant version:

Email everyone the same Google review link
Send a separate satisfaction survey to capture internal feedback
You don't filter who sees the Google link, but you capture private feedback in parallel
I'd teach BOTH versions in the video and let viewers choose. The "filtered" version converts way better but has policy risk. The "compliant" version is safer.

Tech stack for either:

GHL or Typeform for the form
Make.com for the routing logic
Claude Code generates the email copy + form questions
3. Keep the "how to sell this" section — 100%

Without it, this is a tutorial. With it, it's a business opportunity. Your audience is freelancers who watch your videos to make money — they're not learning local SEO for fun. Cutting it would gut the value proposition.

But: tighten it. 3 minutes max instead of 4. Just the essentials — pricing, what you deliver, how long setup takes, the multi-location unlock.

<script>
  const slides = [
    // INTRO
    { file: '00-title.html',              chapter: 'Intro',  title: 'Local SEO Masterclass' },

    { file: '04-magic-ten.html',          chapter: 'Part 1', title: 'The magic 10 reviews' },

    // PART 2 - GBP OPTIMIZATION
    { file: 'part-2-divider.html',        chapter: 'Part 2', title: 'GBP optimization' },

    { file: '06-services-section.html',   chapter: 'Part 2', title: 'Services section' },
    { file: '07-reviews-engine.html',     chapter: 'Part 2', title: 'The review engine' },

    // PART 4 - HYPERLOCAL BLOG
    { file: 'part-4-divider.html',        chapter: 'Part 4', title: 'Hyperlocal blog engine' },
    { file: '17-blog-engine.html',        chapter: 'Part 4', title: 'The "best X in [city]" engine' },
    { file: '18-blog-examples.html',      chapter: 'Part 4', title: 'Real-world examples' },

    // PART 5 - CLAUDE CODE
    { file: 'part-5-divider.html',        chapter: 'Part 5', title: 'Claude Code automation' },
    { file: '19-claude-posts.html',       chapter: 'Part 5', title: 'GBP post generation' },
    { file: '20-claude-reviews.html',     chapter: 'Part 5', title: 'Review response generation' },
    { file: '21-claude-pages.html',       chapter: 'Part 5', title: 'Location pages at scale' },
    { file: '22-claude-schema.html',      chapter: 'Part 5', title: 'Schema markup generator' },

    { file: '29-multi-location.html',     chapter: 'Part 7', title: 'The multi-location unlock' },

    // CTA
    { file: '30-cta.html',                chapter: 'Outro',  title: 'Your next step' }
  ];

  const $slide  = document.getElementById('slide');
  const $count  = document.getElementById('count');
  const $title  = document.getElementById('title');
  const $bar    = document.getElementById('bar');
  const $dots   = document.getElementById('dots');
  const $hud    = document.getElementById('hud');
  const $menu   = document.getElementById('menu');
  const $menuBackdrop = document.getElementById('menuBackdrop');
  const $menuBtn      = document.getElementById('menuBtn');
  const $menuClose    = document.getElementById('menuClose');
  const $menuList     = document.getElementById('menuList');

  let current = 0;

  slides.forEach((_, i) => {
    const btn = document.createElement('button');
    btn.className = 'dot';
    btn.setAttribute('aria-label', `Slide ${i + 1}`);
    btn.addEventListener('click', () => go(i));
    $dots.appendChild(btn);
  });

  slides.forEach((s, i) => {
    const btn = document.createElement('button');
    btn.className = 'row';
    btn.innerHTML = `<span class="num">${i + 1}</span><span><span class="chapter">${s.chapter}</span>${s.title}</span>`;
    btn.addEventListener('click', () => { go(i); closeMenu(); });
    $menuList.appendChild(btn);
  });

  function go(i) {
    current = (i + slides.length) % slides.length;
    const s = slides[current];
    $slide.classList.add('fading');
    setTimeout(() => { $slide.src = s.file; $slide.classList.remove('fading'); }, 160);
    $count.textContent = `${current + 1} / ${slides.length}`;
    $title.textContent = `${s.chapter} — ${s.title}`;
    $bar.style.width = ((current + 1) / slides.length * 100) + '%';
    $dots.querySelectorAll('.dot').forEach((d, idx) => d.classList.toggle('active', idx === current));
    $menuList.querySelectorAll('.row').forEach((r, idx) => r.classList.toggle('active', idx === current));
    history.replaceState(null, '', '#' + (current + 1));
  }
  function next() { go(current + 1); }
  function prev() { go(current - 1); }
  function openMenu() { $menu.classList.add('open'); $menuBackdrop.classList.add('open'); $menu.setAttribute('aria-hidden', 'false'); }
  function closeMenu() { $menu.classList.remove('open'); $menuBackdrop.classList.remove('open'); $menu.setAttribute('aria-hidden', 'true'); }

  document.getElementById('prev').addEventListener('click', prev);
  document.getElementById('next').addEventListener('click', next);
  $menuBtn.addEventListener('click', openMenu);
  $menuClose.addEventListener('click', closeMenu);
  $menuBackdrop.addEventListener('click', closeMenu);

  document.addEventListener('keydown', (e) => {
    if (e.target.tagName === 'INPUT' || e.target.tagName === 'TEXTAREA') return;
    switch (e.key) {
      case 'ArrowRight': e.preventDefault(); next(); break;
      case 'ArrowLeft': e.preventDefault(); prev(); break;
      case 'f': case 'F': e.preventDefault(); if (!document.fullscreenElement) document.documentElement.requestFullscreen(); else document.exitFullscreen(); break;
      case 'm': case 'M': e.preventDefault(); if ($menu.classList.contains('open')) closeMenu(); else openMenu(); break;
      case 'Escape': if ($menu.classList.contains('open')) closeMenu(); break;
    }
  });

  let idleTimer;
  function resetIdle() { $hud.classList.remove('idle'); clearTimeout(idleTimer); idleTimer = setTimeout(() => $hud.classList.add('idle'), 2600); }
  document.addEventListener('mousemove', resetIdle);
  document.addEventListener('keydown', resetIdle);
  document.addEventListener('click', resetIdle);
  resetIdle();

  const initial = parseInt((location.hash || '#1').slice(1), 10);
  go(Number.isFinite(initial) && initial >= 1 && initial <= slides.length ? initial - 1 : 0);
</script>
</body>
</html>

    <div class="eyebrow">Chapter 16 · The hidden ranking trap</div>
    <h1>The <span class="mark">URL you link from GBP</span> matters more than people think.</h1>
    <div class="subhead">Link your GBP to a page already ranking organically and <strong>Google may demote your profile</strong> to avoid showing you twice for the same query. Almost no one talks about this.</div>
  </div>

  <div class="canvas url-grid">

    <div class="card url-card">
      <span class="url-tag bad">⚠️ THE TRAP</span>

      <div class="gbp-link">
        <span class="label">GBP website link points to</span>
        <div class="url-input bad">
          <span class="protocol">https://</span>
          <span class="path">acmeplumbing.com/</span>
          <span style="color: var(--stamp); font-weight: 800;">(homepage)</span>
        </div>
      </div>

      <div class="conflict-card">
        <span class="ic">⚠️</span>
        <span class="text">Homepage already ranks <b>#2 organically</b> for "plumber toronto." Google demotes the GBP listing to avoid duplicate dominance.</span>
      </div>

      <div class="arrow-down"><span class="a">↓</span></div>

      <div class="ranking-row bad">
        <div>
          <div class="rk-label">GBP rank</div>
          <div class="rk-num">#8</div>
        </div>
        <div class="rk-context">Demoted because the linked page is already ranking. Your traffic suffers.</div>
      </div>
    </div>

    <div class="card url-card" style="border-color: var(--ink); border-width: 3px;">
      <span class="url-tag good">✓ THE FIX</span>

      <div class="gbp-link">
        <span class="label">GBP website link points to</span>
        <div class="url-input">
          <span class="protocol">https://</span>
          <span class="path">acmeplumbing.com/plumber/<b style="color: var(--good);">toronto</b></span>
        </div>
      </div>

      <div class="clean-card">
        <span class="ic">✓</span>
        <span class="text">Dedicated <b>location landing page</b> for Toronto. Not competing with itself organically. Both can rank.</span>
      </div>

      <div class="arrow-down"><span class="a">↓</span></div>

      <div class="ranking-row good">
        <div>
          <div class="rk-label">GBP rank</div>
          <div class="rk-num">#1</div>
        </div>
        <div class="rk-context">Top local pack AND organic. Both spots, double visibility.</div>
      </div>
    </div>

  </div>

  <div class="key-insight">
    <span class="ic">🎯</span>
    <span class="text"><b>Rule of thumb:</b> Link each GBP profile to a city-specific landing page — never the homepage. Check the ranking of your linked page first with <b>Google Search Console</b>. If it ranks well organically, change the GBP URL to a different page.</span>
  </div>

</div></div></body></html>

Ok, some questions:
📢
GBP Posts (for rankings)
The myth: "Post weekly to GBP and watch your rankings climb."
📊
Sterling Sky 9-week controlled study: zero measurable ranking impact in the local pack from posts.
📉
Average post CTR: 0.5%. Most of your audience won't even see them.


Don't GBPs get you additional traffic? they just don't rank you
You're right — that framing is too dismissive. Posts do drive value, just not the value most courses claim. Here's the accurate breakdown:

What posts DON'T do:

Move you up in the local pack (Sterling Sky study confirmed)
What posts DO drive:

Engagement from people already viewing your profile — they see your latest offer and call instead of bouncing
Branded search visibility — when someone Googles "Acme Plumbing," your latest post shows up in the knowledge panel right there
Offer redemption — "Limited Time Offer" tags make people act faster
"Active profile" signal — recency tells customers the business is alive and operating
GBP click-through to your website — posts have their own CTAs that drive traffic
The slide should say: "Don't post for rankings. Post for conversion." Not "skip posts entirely."

Want me to fix the slide? I'd reframe it as:

Move "GBP Posts" out of the SKIP section
Keep Q&A as the only true SKIP (since Google killed it)
Add a new slide or split this into "What posts actually do" — separating the myth (rankings) from the truth (conversion + branded visibility)
Want me to update slide 10 with the cleaner framing?

  .decision-strip .ic { font-size: 26px; }
  .decision-strip .lbl { font-size: 10px; font-weight: 800; letter-spacing: 0.18em; text-transform: uppercase; color: var(--highlight); }
  .decision-strip .text { font-size: 13px; color: rgba(255,255,255,0.9); line-height: 1.45; flex: 1; }
  .decision-strip .text b { color: var(--highlight); font-weight: 800; }
</style></head>
<body><div class="stage"><div class="frame">

  <div class="head">
    <div class="eyebrow">Lesson 1 · The strategic question</div>
    <h1>One GBP or <span class="mark">seven</span>?</h1>
    <div class="subhead">If you serve 7 cities, do you need 7 GBPs or just 1? <strong>The answer depends on whether you have physical locations</strong> — and getting it wrong = suspension.</div>
  </div>

  <div class="canvas options-grid">

    <div class="card option-card lead">
      <span class="opt-tag b">OPTION A · MULTIPLE GBPs</span>
      <div class="opt-name">7 physical locations · 7 profiles</div>
      <div class="opt-sub">Each location has its own GBP, own address, own phone, own reviews.</div>

      <div class="map-vis">
        <div class="map-pin pin-tor"><span class="lbl">Toronto</span></div>
        <div class="map-pin pin-mis"><span class="lbl">Mississauga</span></div>
        <div class="map-pin pin-bra"><span class="lbl">Brampton</span></div>
        <div class="map-pin pin-vau"><span class="lbl">Vaughan</span></div>
        <div class="map-pin pin-mar"><span class="lbl">Markham</span></div>
        <div class="map-pin pin-sca"><span class="lbl">Scarborough</span></div>
        <div class="map-pin pin-nyk"><span class="lbl">North York</span></div>
      </div>

      <div class="pros-cons">
        <div class="pc-row"><span class="ic good">✓</span><span class="nm"><b>Rank in the local pack for each city.</b> Each profile competes locally.</span></div>
        <div class="pc-row"><span class="ic good">✓</span><span class="nm">7× the impressions, 7× the call/direction actions.</span></div>
        <div class="pc-row"><span class="ic good">✓</span><span class="nm"><b>Multi-location service contracts</b> = bigger retainers.</span></div>
        <div class="pc-row"><span class="ic bad">✗</span><span class="nm">Requires <b>real physical addresses</b> in each city. Co-working ≠ valid.</span></div>
        <div class="pc-row"><span class="ic bad">✗</span><span class="nm">7× the management work — automation is mandatory.</span></div>
      </div>
    </div>

    <div class="card option-card">
      <span class="opt-tag a">OPTION B · SINGLE SAB</span>
      <div class="opt-name">1 location · 7 service areas</div>
      <div class="opt-sub">Service Area Business: one address (hidden), serves up to 20 cities.</div>

      <div class="map-vis">
        <div class="radius-circle"></div>
        <div class="map-pin single-pin"><span class="lbl">Headquarters</span></div>
      </div>

      <div class="pros-cons">
        <div class="pc-row"><span class="ic good">✓</span><span class="nm"><b>One profile to manage.</b> One review pile. One set of photos.</span></div>
        <div class="pc-row"><span class="ic good">✓</span><span class="nm">Legitimate for trades that travel: plumbing, HVAC, mobile detailing.</span></div>
        <div class="pc-row"><span class="ic bad">✗</span><span class="nm"><b>You only rank near your verified address.</b> Service areas don't affect ranking — they're just descriptive.</span></div>
        <div class="pc-row"><span class="ic bad">✗</span><span class="nm">Address is hidden — looks <b>less trustworthy</b> to customers.</span></div>
        <div class="pc-row"><span class="ic bad">✗</span><span class="nm">Compete with all local-pack winners <b>from a single starting point</b>.</span></div>
      </div>
    </div>

  </div>

  <div class="decision-strip">
    <span class="ic">🎯</span>
    <div>
      <div class="lbl">Decision rule</div>
      <div class="text">Got <b>real physical offices?</b> Use multiple GBPs. <b>Mobile/home-based service?</b> Single SAB. <b>Never invent fake addresses</b> — auto-suspension. The franchise / multi-location play is where the real money is.</div>
    </div>
  </div>

</div></div></body></html>

    <div class="eyebrow">Lesson 2 · Important reframe</div>
    <h1>Posts don't rank you. <span class="mark">They convert visitors</span>.</h1>
    <div class="subhead">Most local SEO content claims weekly posts boost rankings. <strong>Real data says they don't.</strong> But posts still drive serious conversion — just for a different reason than people think.</div>
  </div>

  <div class="top-row">

      <span class="myth-tag bad">⚠ THE MYTH</span>
      <div class="myth-headline">"Post weekly and rankings climb."</div>
      <div class="myth-detail">Every "local SEO checklist" repeats this. <b>It's not true.</b></div>
      <div class="study-row bad">
        <span class="stat">0%</span>
        <span class="text"><b>Sterling Sky 9-week controlled study:</b> zero measurable ranking lift in the local pack from posts.</span>
      </div>
    </div>

    <div class="card myth-card good">
      <span class="myth-tag good">✓ THE REALITY</span>
      <div class="myth-headline">Posts drive <b>conversion</b>, not rankings.</div>
      <div class="myth-detail">Profile visitors who see an active, current post <b>are more likely to take action</b>. Branded searches show your latest post in the knowledge panel. <b>Don't skip them — just understand what they do.</b></div>
      <div class="study-row">
        <span class="stat" style="color: var(--highlight);">+22%</span>
        <span class="text"><b>Call-through rate uplift</b> for profiles with current posts vs profiles with stale ones. Posts close, not rank.</span>
      </div>
    </div>
  </div>

  <div class="bottom-section">

        <span class="benefit-lbl">Drives</span>

        <span class="benefit-desc">Someone already on your profile sees <b>"$50 off this week"</b> and calls instead of bouncing.</span>
        <span class="stat">~0.5% CTR</span>

        <span class="benefit-ic">🔍</span>
        <span class="benefit-lbl">Drives</span>
        <span class="benefit-title">Branded search visibility</span>

SEMRush for local SEO — yes, this is massive
SEMRush has a full Local SEO toolkit that's actually the single best reason to include them in this video. Their Listing Management tool replaces ~30 hours of manual citation work:

What SEMRush actually does:
1. Listing Management (the killer feature)

One form → syncs NAP across 70+ directories (Yelp, Apple Maps, Bing Places, Foursquare, BBB, Facebook, Yellow Pages, plus industry-specific)
Auto-detects + fixes NAP inconsistencies
Catches duplicate listings (a common suspension trigger)
Auto-pushes updates everywhere when you change hours, phone, address
~$20/mo per location
2. Map Rank Tracker

Geo-grid heatmap — see your rank from every block in a city
Tracks local pack position across all your target cities
Way better than just "what's our average rank" — shows you the dead zones
3. Review Management

Pulls reviews from Google + Facebook + Yelp into one inbox
Reply from one place
Sentiment trends over time
4. Position Tracking (local mode)

Tracks local SERP rankings
Tells you when AI Overviews appear for your queries
Competitor benchmarking
5. Local SEO Audit

Scans GBP for missing fields
Compares your profile to top-3 competitors
Surfaces gaps
Where they fit naturally in the video:
Lesson	SEMRush feature	Why it fits
Lesson 1 (GBP setup)	Local SEO Audit + competitor research	Compare your GBP to top-3 competitors, find gaps
Lesson 1 (Citations slide)	Listing Management	"Or skip the 30-hour manual citation grind — SEMRush pushes to 70+ directories from one form" — this is the natural hero placement
Lesson 2 (Posts)	Keyword Magic Tool	Find what keywords to target in your post copy
Lesson 4 (Blog content)	Keyword Magic + Topic Research	Find "best X in [city]" terms with real volume
Audit / Prospecting	Map Rank Tracker + Local SEO Audit	Geo-grid screenshots show ranking proof to clients · audit finds prospects
Sell-it (Prospect scraper)	Local SEO Audit on prospects	Run their tool on prospect businesses to find weak GBPs to pitch

Your question on Make.com reporting
Yes — you absolutely can. Make.com's GBP module has a "Get a Location" + "List Insights" action. It returns:

Search impressions (last 30/60/90 days)
Map views
Direction requests
Phone calls
Website clicks
So you can pull the data, dump it into Claude, and Claude writes the narrative report. No API approval needed. This is a great single slide — "you don't need a $300 reporting tool, you need 4 Make.com modules."

I'll add one Lesson 6 slide for this. Not a full reporting deep dive — just "here's how to pull GBP performance + have Claude summarize it."

Your question on AI Overviews — what it actually means
The slide should say:

When someone searches "best plumber in Toronto," Google now generates an AI summary at the top of the results — appearing 40% of the time. It writes the summary by pulling from:

Your GBP profile (description, services, attributes)
Your reviews (sentiment + keywords)
Your citations (Yelp, BBB, etc.)
Your website content (FAQ, location pages)
Distance has zero correlation. A complete profile 10 miles away beats a sparse one across the street.

    <h1>Past customers = <span class="mark">free reviews waiting</span> to be asked.</h1>

          <div class="step-nm">Pull past customer list from CRM</div>
          <div class="step-desc">Last 6-12 months from <b>GHL / Square / Jobber / HubSpot</b> — anyone who paid an invoice. Make.com handles the export.</div>
        </div>
      </div>
